$\tau_{g,n}(\cA) :=
\sum_\Gamma |\operatorname{Aut}(\Gamma)|^{-1}\,
\iota_{\Gamma,*}(\prod_e P_e)\,
w_\Gamma^{\mathrm{cyc}}(\cA)
\in R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n+1})$.
Tautological by construction.
$\tau_{g,2} = \kappa \cdot \pi^*\lambda_g$.
Clutching-compatible via MC factorization.
Additive under independent tensor products.
For affine $V_k(\fg)$:
$\tau_{0,3} = (k{+}h^\vee)^{-1}\sum_\sigma
f^{a_{\sigma(1)}a_{\sigma(2)}c}\kappa^{cd}
f^{da_{\sigma(3)}a_{\sigma(4)}} \cdot
[\mathrm{pt}_\sigma]$
(Example~\ref{ex:tau-03-affine}).

\paragraph{Chriss--Ginzburg tautological programme.}
The shadow tautological classes $\tau_{g,n}(\cA)$
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-tautological-classes},
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tautological-ring})
carry CohFT structure on
$R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n+1})$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-cohft});
the CohFT axioms (flat identity, equivariance, splitting) are formal consequences of $D_\cA^2 = 0$ on the modular bar complex.
The MC factorization
$\xi^*\Theta_\cA = \Theta_\cA \star \Theta_\cA$
descends to tautological relations via
Theorem~\ref{thm:mc-tautological-descent}.
At genus~$0$: WDVV equations = Jacobi identity of the MC bracket
(Proposition~\ref{prop:wdvv-from-mc}).
At arity~$2$: Mumford $\lambda$-class relations from the MC equation
(Proposition~\ref{prop:mumford-from-mc}).
Reconstruction:
the Givental $R$-matrix equals the complementarity propagator
$P_\cA$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:cohft-reconstruction}).
The dressed propagator coefficient
$P^R(D_+,D_-)$ from the edge integral
$\int R(\psi_+)\,R(\psi_-)/(\psi_+ + \psi_-)$
satisfies $P^R(D_+,D_-)=P^R(D_-,D_+)$
(algebraic proof from the symplectic condition
$R(-z)R(z)=1$;
Proposition~\ref{prop:dressed-propagator-resolution}).
The shadow tower free energy on the uniform-weight lane
$F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$
is the Hodge-lambda integral
$\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,1}}\lambda_g\psi^{2g-2}$
(Theorem~D);
the $\psi$-class CohFT graph sum at $(g,0)$
computes a structurally different quantity,
as documented in
Remark~\ref{rem:dressed-propagator-convention}
($44$~compute tests).
Eynard--Orantin topological recursion is the scalar shadow
of the MC tautological relation
(Corollary~\ref{cor:topological-recursion-mc-shadow}).
The Vol~II holographic tautological action
(Definition~\ref{def:descendant-taut-action})
admits a shadow-tower construction from Vol~I data
(Proposition~\ref{prop:correlator-from-shadow-tower}):
the scalar trace of the universal correlator class
$\mathcal{U}_{g,n}^{\cT;B}$ recovers the Vol~I shadow
tautological class $\tau_{g,n}(\cA_\partial(\cT))$.

\paragraph{Non-perturbative shadow partition function.}
\index{shadow partition function!double convergence}
The shadow partition function
$Z^{\mathrm{sh}}(\cA,\hbar) = \sum_{g,r}\hbar^{2g-2}Z_g^{(r)}(\cA)$
converges absolutely for $|\hbar|<2\pi$ and $\rho(\cA)<1$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-double-convergence}).
The bound factorizes: genus decay
$1/(2\pi)^{2g}$ (Bernoulli, Proposition~\ref{prop:fp-genus-decay-for-double})
times arity decay $\rho^r r^{-5/2}$ (shadow radius,
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-radius}).
This contrasts with the \emph{divergent}
string genus expansion ($\sim(2g)!$, Mirzakhani):
the shadow CohFT extracts tautological intersections with
Bernoulli decay, not Weil--Petersson volumes.
Virasoro at $c=26$: $\rho\approx 0.234$, deep in the convergent
regime ($41$~compute tests).

\begin{remark}[Pixton relations from the MC element]
\label{rem:pixton-from-mc}
\index{Pixton relations!from MC element}
\index{tautological relations!Pixton ideal}
The Pixton relations~\cite{Janda17,PPZ19} are a complete set of
tautological relations in $R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n})$ for
$g \geq 2$.  The MC tautological descent
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc-tautological-descent}) produces relations at each
$(g,n)$; the question is whether these generate the Pixton ideal.

At genus~$2$: the MC relation at $(2,0)$ from the three-shell
decomposition
(Construction~\ref{const:vol1-genus-two-shells}) gives
\[
  \Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}^2}
  + \Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}
  + \Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}
  = 0,
\]
which is the genus-$2$ projection of the full MC equation $D\Theta_\cA + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta_\cA, \Theta_\cA] = 0$, and projects to a relation in
$R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_2)$.
For class-G algebras (Heisenberg), only the iterated-loop shell
survives, and the projected relation is the genus-$2$ Mumford
relation $\lambda_2^2 = 0$.  For class-M algebras (Virasoro),
all three shells contribute, and the planted-forest shell
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}$ produces the first non-Mumford
tautological relation; this should be compared with the
Faber--Zagier relation in $R^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_2)$.
\end{remark}

\begin{conjecture}[Pixton ideal from shadow tower; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:pixton-from-shadows}
\index{Pixton relations!generation conjecture}
For class-M algebras with $r_{\max} = \infty$, the infinite family
of MC-descended tautological relations generates the Pixton ideal
in $R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n})$.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Status of Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows}]
\label{rem:pixton-conjecture-status}
\index{Pixton relations!conjecture status|textbf}

\emph{Rank-$1$ primary line.}
For rank-$1$ semisimple ($S_3 \neq 0$):
Givental--Teleman gives $R = 1$, so the shadow CohFT equals the
Witten--Kontsevich CohFT.  The MC relations are the WK relations,
which generate the Pixton ideal by~\cite{PPZ19}.
For rank-$1$ non-semisimple ($S_3 = 0$, Heisenberg):
$\delta_{\mathrm{pf}} = 0$ by direct computation.
The conjecture is satisfied trivially at rank~$1$.

\emph{Principal $\cW$-algebras.}
For $\cW_N = \cW_k(\mathfrak{sl}_N, f_{\mathrm{princ}})$:
the shadow CohFT on $V = \{T, W_3, \ldots, W_N\}$ is the
$A_{N-1}$ Frobenius manifold CohFT
(Feigin--Frenkel identification of the $\cW$-algebra
associated variety with the $A_{N-1}$ singularity).
For semisimple levels: Givental--Teleman identifies this with the
$(N{+}1)$-spin CohFT.
The proof chain
\[
\text{MC equations}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\text{Witten}\;}\;
\text{KdV hierarchy}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\text{FSZ}\;}\;
\text{$r$-spin relations}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\text{PPZ}\;}\;
\text{Pixton ideal}
\]
shows: the MC-descended relations from $\cW_N$ generate the Pixton
ideal.  This proves
Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows} for all principal
$\cW$-algebras at semisimple levels.

For $\cW_3$: the rank-$2$ planted-forest is
$(932 - 7c^2)/(48c^3)$
(eq.~\eqref{eq:w3-planted-forest-genus2}), the $A_2$ $R$-matrix
has off-diagonal $R_1 = -3\sqrt{6}/(8s^2)$ (solved from the
quantum differential equation), and the genus-$2$ free energy
$F_2 = s^2/864 + 7/(51840 s^4)$ receives an $11.7\%$ $R$-correction
over WK.

\emph{Semisimple case: upgraded to theorem.}
The $r$-spin chain is not needed.  The argument generalises:
if the genus-$0$ shadow data defines a \emph{semisimple}
Frobenius algebra on~$V$, then
(a)~Givental--Teleman~\cite{Givental01,Teleman12} reconstructs the
unique semisimple CohFT extending this Frobenius structure, and
(b)~Pandharipande--Pixton--Zvonkine~\cite{PPZ19} prove that any
semisimple CohFT generates the Pixton ideal.
Since the MC equation at each $(g,n)$ produces a tautological relation
of this CohFT
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc-tautological-descent}), and the CohFT is
uniquely determined by its genus-$0$ data, the MC relations at all
$(g,n)$ encode exactly the CohFT's tautological content.

This proves Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows} for
\emph{all chirally Koszul algebras whose genus-$0$ shadow data
defines a semisimple Frobenius algebra}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:planted-forest-structure}(vi)).
This includes: all principal $\cW_N$ at non-critical levels,
subregular $\cW$-algebras
(associated variety = $D_{N-1}$ singularity), hook-type
in type~$A$, and more generally any $\cW_k(\fg,f)$ whose
Slodowy slice gives a simple or semisimple singularity at
generic~$k$.

\emph{Non-semisimple frontier.}
The conjecture remains genuinely open for:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item
  Logarithmic/non-rational algebras (e.g., $\cW(p)$ triplet algebras)
  where the Frobenius algebra is non-semisimple;
  Givental--Teleman does not apply and the CohFT lives in the
  coderived category.
\item
  Admissible-level simple quotients $L_k(\fg)$ where vacuum null
  vectors collapse the Frobenius algebra to a non-semisimple quotient.
\item
  Algebras outside the Koszul locus where the shadow CohFT
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-cohft}) may not exist.
\end{itemize}
The non-semisimple case requires the
Pandharipande--Pixton--Zvonkine framework to be extended to
non-semisimple CohFTs, or an independent structural argument from
the MC equation's planted-forest structure
(Remark~\ref{rem:non-semisimple-cohft}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Computational evidence: genus-$2$ planted-forest correction]
\label{rem:pixton-genus2-computation}
\index{Pixton relations!genus-2 planted-forest}
\index{planted-forest correction!explicit genus-2 formula}
At genus~$2$ with $n = 0$, the planted-forest correction
$\delta_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(2,0)}$ receives contributions from
four stable graphs of codimension~${\geq}\,2$:
the sunset~$C$ (codim~$2$, weight~$S_4$),
the bridge-loop~$E$ (codim~$2$, weight~$S_3\kappa$),
the theta~$F$ (codim~$3$, weight~$S_3^2$),
and the figure-$8$ bridge~$G$ (codim~$3$, weight~$S_3^2$).
Graph~$C$ has vanishing Hodge integral.
The remaining three yield
\begin{equation}\label{eq:planted-forest-genus2-polynomial}
\delta_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(2,0)}
\;=\;
\frac{S_3(10S_3 - \kappa)}{48},
\end{equation}
a factored polynomial in the modular characteristic~$\kappa = S_2$
and cubic shadow~$S_3$.
For class-$\mathsf{G}$ algebras ($S_3 = 0$):
$\delta_{\mathrm{pf}} = 0$, recovering pure Mumford.
For the Virasoro algebra ($\kappa = c/2$, $S_3 = 2$):
$\delta_{\mathrm{pf}} = -(c-40)/48$,
vanishing at~$c = 40$ and changing sign there.
Verified numerically at $c = 1, 2, 10, 13, 25, 26$
(\texttt{pixton\_shadow\_bridge.py}, $75$ tests).

At genus~$3$, the complete planted-forest correction (from
$19$~stable graphs: $4$ one-vertex, $12$ two-vertex, $3$ three-vertex
star) is an $8$-term polynomial in $\kappa, S_3, S_4, S_5$
(eq.~\eqref{eq:delta-pf-genus3-explicit}).
The quartic~$S_4$ and quintic~$S_5$ enter for the first time;
$S_6$ remains invisible (the pure-self-loop $(0,6)$ graph has
vanishing Hodge integral by
Proposition~\ref{prop:self-loop-vanishing}).

The self-loop parity vanishing theorem
(Proposition~\ref{prop:self-loop-vanishing}) shows that
pure-self-loop graphs $(0,2k)$ vanish for all $k \geq 2$,
forcing the shadow visibility genus
$g_{\min}(S_r) = \lfloor r/2 \rfloor + 1$
(Corollary~\ref{cor:shadow-visibility-genus}):
two new shadow coefficients enter at each genus.
At genus~$g$, the planted-forest involves~$S_r$
for $3 \leq r \leq 2g{-}1$.

\emph{Class-level visibility.}
The integrated visibility genus
$g_{\min}(S_r) = \lfloor r/2 \rfloor + 1$
underestimates the class-level visibility.
The cyclic marking converts a $(0,2k)$ vertex to
$(0,2k{+}1)$ with even dimension, defeating
the parity obstruction of
Proposition~\ref{prop:self-loop-vanishing}.
In particular, the descendant pairing
$\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{2,1}}
\delta_{\mathrm{pf}}\,\psi_1^2
= S_3\kappa/48 + S_4/8$
reveals $S_4$ at genus~$2$ at the class level
(Remark~\ref{rem:class-vs-integrated-visibility}).

\emph{Pixton universality test.}
The boundary correlator
$\langle\tau_4\rangle_2^{\mathrm{boundary}} = 1/1152$
is shadow-independent, equalling the Witten--Kontsevich
intersection number.
This verifies the strongest computationally testable
Pixton constraint: the top-degree boundary contribution
is universal ($82$~tests).

\emph{Rank-$1$ triviality and rank-$2$ frontier.}
For rank-$1$ on the primary line, Givental--Teleman gives
$R = 1$, so the shadow CohFT equals the Witten--Kontsevich CohFT and
\textup{conj:pixton-from-shadows} is automatically satisfied
(the MC relations are WK relations).
The non-trivial content of the conjecture requires \emph{higher rank}.

For $\cW_3$ (rank~$2$, generators $T,W$ with $\mathbb{Z}_2$~symmetry
$W \to -W$), the Frobenius algebra on $V = \{T,W\}$ has
$T{*}T = (4/c)\,T$, $T{*}W = (6/c)\,W$, $W{*}W = (4/c)\,T$,
which is semisimple with eigenvalues $4/c \neq 6/c$.
The Givental $R$-matrix is $R \neq I$ (it is the $A_2$ singularity
$R$-matrix).  The rank-$2$ genus-$2$ planted-forest is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-planted-forest-genus2}
\delta_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(2,0)}(\cW_3)
\;=\;
\frac{932 - 7c^2}{48\,c^3},
\end{equation}
using $S_3(T,T,T) = 2$, $S_3(T,W,W) = 1$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-archetype-classification}),
$\eta = \operatorname{diag}(c/2, c/3)$,
$\kappa_W = 0$ ($\mathbb{Z}_2$~symmetry).
This differs from the rank-$1$ formula $(40{-}c)/48$ by a
$W$-channel correction from the spin-$3$ field
propagating through internal graph edges.
The $3$-spin correlator
$\langle\tau_1\rangle_{2,1}^{3\mathrm{-spin}} = 1/1620
\neq 1/1152 = \langle\tau_4\rangle_{2,1}^{\mathrm{WK}}$
confirms the CohFT is genuinely non-WK.

\emph{Caveat.}
At genus~$3$, genus-$0$ vertex weights~$S_k$ are exact;
genus-$1{+}$ vertex weights use
$\ell_2^{(1)} = S_3\kappa/24 - S_3^2$ (exact from MC; Beilinson audit
corrected the $S_3^2$ coefficient from $1/2$ to $1$ after
finding a missing bridge-plus-self-loop graph at $(1,2)$)
and $\ell_3^{(1)} \approx \kappa$ (approximate).
Full Pixton ideal generation at rank~$2$ requires
the strata algebra of $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{2,1}$
at rank~$2$.
\end{remark}

\paragraph{Analytic shadow realization
\textup{(}Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:analytic-shadow-realization}}\textup{)}.}
For all $\cA$ in the standard landscape,
$\barB(\cA) \hookrightarrow \barB^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA)$
densely; finite-arity shadows are algebraic; hence
the algebraic and analytic shadow data coincide.
Follows from HS-sewing
(Theorem~\ref{thm:general-hs-sewing}).


%% ====================================================================
%%  THE POLYAKOV PROGRAMME
%% ====================================================================
\section{The Polyakov programme}
\label{sec:concordance-polyakov-programme}
\index{Polyakov programme|textbf}
\index{Polyakov formula!concordance}
\index{conformal anomaly!Polyakov programme}

The shadow tower completes Polyakov's functional-integral programme
(1987): every object Polyakov constructs by path-integral methods
has a precise algebraic counterpart in the modular convolution
algebra~$\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA$.

\paragraph{Dictionary.}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{4.8cm}p{5.6cm}l@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Polyakov (1981--87)} & \textbf{Bar-cobar} & \textbf{Status} \\
\midrule
Polyakov formula
  $\log(\det'\!\Delta_{g_1}/\det'\!\Delta_{g_0})$
  & Arity-$2$ shadow~$\kappa(\cA)$
  & Proved \\
Critical dimension $c = 26$
  & Dual modular characteristic
    $\kappa(\cA^!) = 0$
  & Proved \\
Conformal anomaly
  $\langle T^a{}_a \rangle = (c/12)\,R$
  & Modular characteristic~$\kappa(\cA)$
  & Proved \\
Functional determinant $\det'_\zeta\!\Delta$
  & Fredholm determinant $\det(1 - K)$
    on Bergman space
  & Proved \\
Genus expansion
  $Z = \sum_g g_s^{2g-2}\,Z_g$
  & MC5 sewing programme,
    uniform-weight
    $F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$
  & Proved \\
Ghost system $bc$
  ($c_{\mathrm{ghost}} = -26$)
  & Koszul dual~$\cA^!$
  & Proved \\
BPZ equations
  $\nabla^{\mathrm{BPZ}}_c \mathcal{F} = 0$
  & Shadow connection~$\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}}$
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-connection})
  & Proved \\
Instantons (Novikov parameter $q^\beta$)
  & Novikov-completed bar complex
    $B^\Lambda(\cA)$
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:novikov-completion-theorem})
  & Proved (framework) \\
Wilson loop $\langle W(C) \rangle$
  & Swiss-cheese boundary module
  & Structural \\
Gauge/string duality
  & Holographic modular Koszul datum
    $\mathcal{H}(T)$
    (Definition~\ref{def:holographic-modular-koszul-datum})
  & Conjectural programme \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\paragraph{Five main results.}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The Polyakov formula is the arity-$2$ Chern--Weil image
  of the shadow tower
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:polyakov-arity-two-projection}).
\item The critical dimension $c = 26$ is the zero of the dual
  modular characteristic
  $\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}) = 0$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-moduli}).
\item The ghost sector is the Koszul dual:
  $Q_{\mathrm{BRST}} = d_B$, physical states
  $= H^*(\barB(\cA))$
  (Remark~\ref{rem:ghost-koszul-identification}).
\item The genus expansion converges for chiral algebras on
  compact curves, with $|F_g| \sim (2\pi)^{-2g}$
  (Remark~\ref{rem:genus-expansion-convergence-comparison}).
\item Instanton sectors are organized by Novikov-completed
  bar complexes
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:novikov-completion-theorem}).
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Three frontier items.}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Matrix models as discretized shadow towers.}
  The random-surface genus expansion
  $Z = \sum_g N^{2-2g}\,Z_g$ should be a discretization of
  the shadow tower, with the double-scaling limit recovering
  the continuum shadow.
  \hfill\textup{(Conjectural)}
\item \emph{Non-critical string theory as Liouville $+$
  complementarity.}
  The anomaly cancellation
  $c_{\mathrm{matter}} + c_{\mathrm{Liouville}} +
  c_{\mathrm{ghost}} = 0$
  is the ambient complementarity theorem
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:quantum-complementarity-main}).
  \hfill\textup{(Structural)}
\item \emph{Polyakov connection on Teichm\"uller space.}
  The shadow connection~$\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}}$ should define a
  flat connection on the Teichm\"uller space~$\mathcal{T}_g$,
  with monodromy encoding the mapping-class group
  representation.
  \hfill\textup{(To be developed)}
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Bibliographic pointers.}
Polyakov~1981 (Polyakov action),
Belavin--Polyakov--Zamolodchikov~1984 (conformal symmetry),
Belavin--Knizhnik~1986 (factorization on~$\overline{\cM}_g$),
Alvarez~1983 (Polyakov--Alvarez formula).

\paragraph{Cross-references.}
Proposition~\ref{prop:polyakov-arity-two-projection}
(\S\ref{sec:koszul-across-genera});
Remark~\ref{rem:complementarity-polyakov-cancellation}
(\S\ref{sec:complementarity-theorem});
Remark~\ref{rem:ghost-koszul-identification}
(Chapter~\ref{chap:free-fields});
Proposition~\ref{prop:polyakov-chern-weil}
(\S\ref{sec:thqg-perturbative-finiteness}).


\section{Bridges to Volume~II}
\label{sec:cross-volume-bridges}
\index{Volume II!bridges from Volume I}

Volume~II develops the $A_\infty$-chiral Hochschild theory in
three space-time dimensions with the operad
$\mathrm{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$.  Homotopy--Koszulity of
$\mathrm{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is proved in Volume~II
(via Kontsevich formality and transfer from the classical
Swiss--cheese operad), so the bar--cobar adjunction for
$\mathrm{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-algebras is a Quillen
\emph{equivalence}.  Volume~II has \emph{no remaining conjectural
algebraic inputs}; its only conditional inputs are the
standing analytic hypotheses (H1)--(H4).
Five bridges connect the two volumes:

\begin{proposition}[Bar-cobar bridge; \ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere]
\label{conj:vol2-bar-cobar-bridge}%
\label{prop:vol2-bar-cobar-bridge}%
The $\mathrm{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ bar-cobar Quillen equivalence of
Volume~II recovers the chiral bar-cobar adjunction of Theorem~A
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-isomorphism-main}) for boundary
operators of the 3d theory.  The closed color specializes to the BD
chiral operad (Vol~II, associated graded proposition).
\end{proposition}

\begin{conjecture}[Hochschild bridge; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:vol2-hochschild-bridge}
The bulk algebra of the 3d theory is the derived center
$Z_{\mathrm{der}}(\cA^!)$, which identifies with the chiral
Hochschild cochain complex $\operatorname{HH}^*_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA^!)$
via the corrected Koszul triangle
(Vol~II, Theorem~J): $A_{\mathrm{bulk}} \simeq
Z_{\mathrm{der}}(B_\partial) \simeq
\operatorname{HH}^*_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA^!)$,
where $B_\partial := \cA^!$ is the boundary algebra.
This recovers Theorem~H
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-algebra-hochschild}) via dimensional
descent.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proposition}[DK-YBE bridge; \ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere]
\label{conj:vol2-dk-ybe-bridge}%
\label{prop:vol2-dk-ybe-bridge}%
The spectral braiding $r(z) = \int_0^\infty e^{-pz}
\{a_\lambda b\}\,dp$ (the Laplace transform of the
$\lambda$-bracket) recovers the DK-0 chain-level
monodromy comparison (Theorem~\ref{thm:derived-dk-affine}).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[\texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{W}$}{W}-algebra bridge at genus $0$; \ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere]
\label{conj:vol2-w-algebra-bridge}%
\label{prop:vol2-w-algebra-bridge}%
The Feynman $m_k$ operations of the 3d theory, restricted to
the $\mathcal{W}$-algebra family, match the bar differential computed in the
$\mathcal{W}$-algebra chapters of Part~II at genus~$0$.
Extension to genus~$1$ is proved
(Volume~II, genus-one bridge theorem:
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^2 = \kappa(\cA)\cdot\omega_1$ via the Arnold
defect on the torus); extension to $g \geq 2$ is proved algebraically
(Theorem~\ref{thm:inductive-genus-determination}:
inductive genus determination via the bar-intrinsic construction),
with the analytic comparison
(Theorem~\ref{thm:analytic-algebraic-comparison})
established for all graph amplitudes on~$\Sigma_g$
by two-dimensional convergence
(Proposition~\ref{prop:2d-convergence}:
no UV renormalization in dimension~$2$).
The remaining analytic input is HS-sewing
(Definition~\ref{def:hs-sewing}) for the mode-sum
extension from $\cA_{\mathrm{alg}}$ to $\cA^{\mathrm{sew}}$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[Relative holographic deformation bridge;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{prop:vol2-relative-holographic-bridge}%
\index{relative holographic deformation complex!cross-volume bridge}%
The forgetful morphism
$p\colon \mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{SC}}_T \to \gAmod[\cA]$
(Vol~II, Swiss-cheese convolution to Vol~I modular
convolution) has fibre
$\mathfrak{h}_T^\Theta =
\operatorname{fib}(p)_{\alpha_T}$
whose MC elements are lifts of the proved boundary
datum~$\Theta_\cA$ to full $3d$ data
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:lifts-as-relative-mc}}\textup{)}.
The obstruction tower at color depth~$r$ lives in
$H^2(\operatorname{gr}^F_r \mathfrak{h}_T^\Theta)$.
At depth~$4$, the relative quartic obstruction
$\mathfrak{R}_4^{\mathrm{rel}}(T)$ measures failure
of the boundary modular datum to lift to a planar
holographic realization.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[Ribbon/'t~Hooft bridge;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]%
\label{prop:vol2-ribbon-thooft-bridge}%
\index{ribbon structure!cross-volume bridge}%
\index{t Hooft expansion@'t~Hooft expansion!cross-volume bridge}%
The $E_1$ modular Koszul theory of Vol~I
\textup{(}Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:e1-modular-koszul}}\textup{)}
and the Swiss-cheese operad of Vol~II
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:recognition}}\textup{)}
combine as follows:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item bare modular graph sums give genus-organized
  expansions\textup;
\item cyclic trace $+$ matrix realization upgrade these
  to literal 't~Hooft sums with $N^{\chi(\Sigma_\Gamma)}$
  weighting
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:exact-n-chi-weighting}}\textup{)}\textup;
\item the ribbonized modular Swiss-cheese theory
  $\mathrm{RSC}_{\mathrm{tr}}^{\mathrm{mod}}$
  \textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:ribbonized-swiss-cheese}}\textup{)}
  is the correct holographic open/closed 't~Hooft language.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{conjecture}[Loop--Connes bridge; \ClaimStatusConjectured]%
\label{conj:vol2-loop-connes-bridge}%
\index{Loop--Connes principle!cross-volume bridge}%
Closed genus creation \textup{(}the genus-loop operator
$\Lambda_P$ of Vol~I\textup{)} is the image of the open
BV/Connes operator under the derived-center map:
$\beta_{\mathrm{der}}^*(\Delta_{\mathrm{open}})
= \Lambda_P$
\textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:loop-connes-transfer}}\textup{)}.
In words: loops in the bulk are traces on the boundary.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{conjecture}[BV functor bridge; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:vol2-bv-functor-bridge}
Analytic hypotheses (H1)--(H4) of Volume~II define the
physics-to-algebra functor that realizes the
$\mathrm{BV} = \mathrm{bar}$ identification at higher
genus (MC5, Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-bv-brst}).
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[PVA quantization bridge]
\label{rem:concordance-pva-bridge}
\index{Poisson vertex algebra!quantization bridge}%
Volume~II constructs the modular PVA quantization pipeline:
a Poisson vertex algebra $V$ (the classical shadow of a
chiral algebra) determines a stable-graph modular deformation
complex $\mathrm{Def}_{\mathrm{cyc}}^{\mathrm{mod}}(V)$,
and the genus-$1$ obstruction is the variational modular class
$\mathrm{Mod}(V) = [\Delta_{\mathrm{cyc}} P_\Pi]$.
For the $\mathcal{W}_3$ PVA, $\mathrm{Mod}(V) = 0$
(Volume~II, Theorem~N).  The lift freedom is one-dimensional,
generated by the central-parameter direction: the unique
deformation that produces the quantized $\mathcal{W}_3$
at central charge $c = c(k)$.  This connects Volume~II's
PVA descent (Theorem~G) with Volume~I's shadow tower
(the arity-$2$ projection $\Theta_\cA^{\leq 2}$ recovers
the modular characteristic $\kappa(\cA)$, which is the
quantized value of the classical variational class).
\end{remark}


\section[Towards modular homotopy theory]{Towards modular homotopy theory for factorization algebras on curves}
\label{sec:modular-koszul-programme}
\index{modular Koszul duality!project}

The modular characteristic theorem (Theorem~D,
Theorem~\ref{thm:modular-characteristic}) establishes the scalar
logarithmic datum~$\kappa(\cA)$.  This section identifies the six
components (five structural extensions and the Hochschild
cohomology theorem) needed to pass from the proved modular Koszul
core to modular homotopy theory for factorization algebras on
curves; that is, to complete the nilpotence-periodicity
correspondence
(Remark~\ref{rem:nilpotence-periodicity}) from the scalar level to
the full categorical level:

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}cp{4.4cm}p{3.8cm}p{4.6cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Label} & \textbf{Statement} & \textbf{Status} & \textbf{Reference} \\
\midrule
$A_{\mathrm{mod}}$ & Bar-cobar intertwined with Verdier, & \textbf{Proved} & Thm~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-isomorphism-main} \\
  & functorial over $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$ & & \\[2pt]
$B_{\mathrm{mod}}$ & Inversion on Koszul locus; coderived & Proved on Koszul locus; & Thm~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}, \\
  & persistence off it & coderived persistence conjectural & \S\ref{subsec:coderived-ran} \\[2pt]
$C_{\mathrm{mod}}$ & Shifted symplectic complementarity & \textbf{Proved} & Thms~\ref{thm:quantum-complementarity-main}, \\
  & (PTVV Lagrangian embedding) & & \ref{thm:ambient-complementarity-fmp} \\[2pt]
Index & GRR: uniform-weight genus series $= \kappa(\cA) \cdot (\hat{A}(ix) - 1)$; genus-$1$ unconditional & \textbf{Proved} & Thm~\ref{thm:family-index} \\[2pt]
DK & DK-0/1/$1\frac{1}{2}$: chain-level, eval-locus, lattice; & DK-0/1/$1\frac{1}{2}$: proved (all types); & Thms~\ref{thm:derived-dk-affine}, \\
  & DK-2/3: factorization DK; & DK-2/3: \textbf{proved} (eval-gen.\ core, all types, domain: $\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{poly}}$; & \ref{thm:derived-dk-yangian}, \ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}, \\
  & DK-4/5: dg-shifted/triple bridge & uses Molev PBW \cite{molev-yangians}); DK-4: ML proved, alg.\ id.\ open; DK-5: conj. & \ref{thm:dk-fd-typeA}, \ref{cor:dk23-all-types}, \ref{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler}; Conj.~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge} \\[2pt]
$H$ & Chiral Hochschild: $\ChirHoch^*(\Walg^k(\fg)) \cong \mathbb{C}[\Theta_1,\ldots,\Theta_r]$; & \textbf{Proved} (generic level, & Thms~\ref{thm:w-algebra-hochschild}, \\
  & period $2$ (rank $1$), polynomial (rank $\geq 2$); & critical level: ProvedElsewhere) & \ref{thm:virasoro-hochschild}, \ref{thm:critical-level-cohomology}; \\
  & Koszul functoriality via Connes~$S$ & & Thm~\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{remark}[Four levels of modular invariant]%
\label{rem:four-levels}%
\index{modular homotopy theory!four levels}%
The six components above implement a hierarchy of modular
invariants of increasing categorical depth.
The proved scalar level is the lowest;
the full modular homotopy type is the highest:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}clll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Level} & \textbf{Invariant} & \textbf{Type} & \textbf{Status} \\
\midrule
$0$ & $\kappa(\cA) \cdot \hat{A}$-genus
  & Numbers $F_g$ & \textbf{Proved} (Thm~D) \\[2pt]
$1$ & $H^*(\barB^{(g)}(\cA), \Dg{g})$
  & Graded vector spaces & \textbf{Resolved} at integrable levels \\
  & & & (Thm~\ref{thm:bar-cohomology-level-independence}) \\[2pt]
$2$ & Variation of $H^*$ over $\mathcal{M}_g$
  & Flat connection (KZ/Hitchin) & Constructed
  (\S\ref{subsec:primitive-flat-connection}); descent
  conditional on locally-free hypothesis \\[2pt]
$3$ & Factorization and sewing
  & Chain-level modular functor & Structural \\
  & & (Thm~\ref{thm:chain-modular-functor}) & \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Theorem~D is the \emph{integrability condition}:
$\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ is a pure
tautological class, free of boundary or non-tautological
contributions, guaranteeing that the curvature of the genus-$g$
bar complex is absorbable by a period correction.
The corrected complex $(\barB^{(g)}, \Dg{g})$ with
$\Dg{g}^{\,2} = 0$ (Level~$1$) is the
\emph{derived fiber} of the factorization homology bundle
$\int_{\Sigma_g}\!\cA$ over~$\mathcal{M}_g$; its variation
(Level~$2$) recovers the monodromy representation of the mapping
class group; its factorization structure (Level~$3$) recovers the
full modular functor
(Theorem~\ref{thm:chain-modular-functor}).  The $\hat{A}$-genus
is the \emph{first Chern class} of this bundle, its Euler
characteristic, not the bundle itself.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Smoking gun}: for $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ at level~$k$,
$\kappa = 3(k{+}2)/4$ is one number, yet the Verlinde formula
gives a bundle of rank $k{+}1$ at genus~$1$
(equation~\eqref{eq:verlinde-general}), growing with~$g$.
Bar cohomology $H^0(\barB^{(1)}(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_{2,k}),
\Dg{1})$ should recover the Verlinde dimension: a concrete,
computable test that Level~$1$ carries representation-theoretic
data invisible to Level~$0$.  See
\S\ref{subsec:chain-modular-functor}.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Resolution of genus-independence at integrable levels.}
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cohomology-level-independence} proves that
bar cohomology dimensions are polynomial in $\lambda = k + h^\vee$,
constant outside a finite exceptional set~$\Sigma_n$.  For
$\mathfrak{sl}_2$ at degree~$2$: $\Sigma_2 = \{0\}$ (critical level
only).  Since integrable levels $k \ge 1$ give $\lambda \ge 3 > 0$,
they are \emph{generic}, not exceptional, and the fiberwise bar
cohomology is genus-independent there
(Proposition~\ref{prop:integrable-level-independence}).  The
integer conformal block dimension $\dim V_{g,k}$ relates to the
normalized partition function~$Z_g$ via $\dim V = Z_g \cdot
S_{00}^{\,2-2g}$ (Remark~\ref{rem:two-verlinde-normalizations}).
\end{remark}

\noindent
The subsections below develop each component, separating what is
established from what remains.  For $A_{\mathrm{mod}}$: the present
proof establishes functorial compatibility of bar and cobar over
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$; whether this lifts to an equivalence
of modular operads is a further question, not addressed here.

\medskip

\subsection{The coderived Ran-space formalism}
\label{subsec:coderived-ran}

The bar-cobar adjunction is most naturally an equivalence of
$\infty$-categories, the categorical $\exp/\log$ correspondence
(Remark~\ref{rem:nilpotence-periodicity}):
\[
\bar{B}_X \colon
\operatorname{Alg}_{\mathrm{aug}}(\operatorname{Fact}(X))
\;\rightleftarrows\;
\operatorname{CoAlg}_{\mathrm{conil}}(\operatorname{Fact}(X))
\,:\!\Omega_X,
\]
where $\operatorname{Fact}(X)$ denotes factorization algebras on
$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$ (cf.\ Appendix~\ref{app:existence-criteria}).

On the Koszul locus this is an equivalence: $\exp \circ \log = \mathrm{id}$
on the convergence domain.  When curvature is present (that is,
when the categorical logarithm acquires non-trivial monodromy), the
correct ambient category is not the ordinary derived category but the
\emph{coderived category} in the sense of
Positselski~\cite{Positselski11}: the analytic continuation that
extends the $\exp/\log$ correspondence past the convergence radius.

Curved objects produce acyclic-but-not-contractible complexes that the
derived category erases too brutally; the coderived category retains
the monodromy data that the ordinary derived category discards, just
as the multi-valued logarithm retains branch information that a
single-valued determination loses.

The provisional coderived category
$\mathsf{D}^{\mathrm{co}}_{\mathrm{prov}}(X)$
(Definition~\ref{def:provisional-coderived},
Proposition~\ref{prop:coderived-adequacy})
provides a working substitute within the scope of this monograph.
On the Koszul locus the coderived and derived categories agree.
Bar-cobar inversion there is genus~$0$ unconditional and, at higher
genus, unconditional on the CFT-type standard landscape except
integer-spin $\beta\gamma$ by
Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-propagation}; in general it remains
conditional on axiom~\ref{MK:modular}
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}\textup{)}.

\emph{Non-circular logical chain.}
The logical foundation for bar-cobar inversion at all genera
is free of circularity
(Remark~\ref{rem:non-circular-logical-chain}).
The antecedent
hypotheses~\ref{MK:koszul}--\ref{MK:modular}
(Definition~\ref{def:modular-koszul-chiral}) are verified
\emph{independently} of bar-cobar inversion: genus-$0$ Koszulity
by the fundamental theorem of chiral twisting morphisms
(Theorem~\ref{thm:fundamental-twisting-morphisms}); Verdier
compatibility by Theorem~\ref{thm:verdier-bar-cobar}; PBW
concentration at all genera by direct spectral-sequence arguments
(Theorems~\ref{thm:pbw-allgenera-km}--\ref{thm:pbw-allgenera-principal-w}).
Given these antecedents, Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}
proves inversion by induction on genus via the stratum-by-stratum
argument of
Lemmas~\ref{lem:higher-genus-open-stratum-qi}--\ref{lem:extension-across-boundary-qi}.
At no point does the proof invoke bar-cobar inversion at the
genus under consideration.

Separately, the bar-intrinsic MC construction
$\Theta_\cA := D_\cA - \dzero$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}) provides Theorems~D
and~H and the shadow Postnikov tower unconditionally,
as projections of a single element whose existence
follows from~$D_\cA^2 = 0$ alone
(Tier~1 of
Remark~\ref{rem:non-circular-logical-chain}).

\emph{PBW propagation and axiom collapse.}
Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-propagation} proves that
axiom~\ref{MK:modular} (PBW concentration at all genera)
\emph{follows from} axiom~\ref{MK:koszul} (genus-$0$
Koszulity) for all CFT-type chiral algebras with positive
conformal grading and a unique weight-$2$ stress tensor.
This covers the entire standard landscape except integer-spin $\beta\gamma$, where the positive-grading hypothesis fails.  The proof
rests on two observations: (i)~the collision differential
is curve-independent (period corrections are regular at
collision diagonals, contributing zero residue);
(ii)~after enrichment killing by $L_0$ invertibility
(Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-universal-semisimple}), the core
spectral sequence at genus~$g$ equals the genus-$0$
spectral sequence.  The five main theorems therefore
follow from genus-$0$ Koszulity and~$D_\cA^2 = 0$ alone
(Remark~\ref{rem:pbw-propagation-scope}).

\emph{What is established.}
Appendix~\ref{app:existence-criteria} compares the strict,
completed, and literature existence paradigms for bar-cobar on
$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.  Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-isomorphism-main}
provides the adjunction; Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}
provides inversion on the Koszul locus.
Appendix~\ref{app:coderived},
\S\ref{subsec:coderived-ran-formalism} develops the coderived
and contraderived categories on~$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$: curved
factorization coalgebras with CDG-factorization compatibility
(Definition~\ref{def:curved-fact-coalgebra}), coacyclic
factorization objects
(Definition~\ref{def:coacyclic-fact}), stratified conservative
restriction via the injective characterization
(Theorem~\ref{thm:stratified-conservative-restriction}),
and the factorization co-contra correspondence
(Theorem~\ref{thm:fact-co-contra-general}).  The provisional
coderived category embeds fully faithfully
(Proposition~\ref{prop:provisional-embedding}).

\emph{Now complete.}
The formerly conjectural off-Koszul bar-cobar inversion on
$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$ is proved
(Theorem~\ref{thm:off-koszul-ran-inversion}): the counit
$\Omega_X \barB_X(\cA) \to \cA$ is an isomorphism in
$D^{\mathrm{co}}(\mathrm{CoFact}(X))$ without Koszulness.
The proof follows the same three-step assembly as
Theorem~\ref{thm:fact-co-contra-general}: (i) on each stratum
$\operatorname{Ran}_n$, Positselski~\cite[Theorem~7.2]{Positselski11}
gives the coderived equivalence for the restricted CDG-coalgebra;
(ii)~factorization compatibility of the bar-cobar counit;
(iii)~conservative assembly via
Theorem~\ref{thm:stratified-conservative-restriction}.
This closes structural gap~H1 and completes Future~2.

\subsection{The Lagrangian form of complementarity}

Theorem~C (Theorem~\ref{thm:quantum-complementarity-main}) establishes
the direct-sum decomposition
$Q_g(\cA) \oplus Q_g(\cA^!)
= H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{Z}(\cA))$
via the eigenspace decomposition of the Verdier involution.
The natural strengthening is a Lagrangian-polarization theorem,
now proved in two layers:

\begin{theorem}[Lagrangian complementarity;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:lagrangian-complementarity}
\index{Lagrangian!complementarity|textbf}
For a modular Koszul pair $(\cA, \cA^!)$, the following hold:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the complex
  $C_g := R\Gamma(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{Z}_{\cA})$
  carries the proved Verdier-side
  $(-(3g{-}3))$-shifted symplectic structure of
  Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:ptvv-lagrangian}}, and
  $Q_g(\cA)$ and $Q_g(\cA^!)$ embed as complementary
  Lagrangians in the sense of
  Pantev--To\"en--Vaqui\'e--Vezzosi~\cite{PTVV13};
\item under the perfectness and nondegeneracy hypotheses of
  Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ambient-complementarity-tangent}(iii)},
  the ambient complementarity formal moduli problem
  $\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{comp}}(\cA)$
  carries a proved $(-1)$-shifted symplectic structure, and
  $\mathcal{M}_{\cA}$ and $\mathcal{M}_{\cA^!}$ define
  complementary Lagrangian maps
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ambient-complementarity-fmp}}\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Degree clarification]\label{rem:lagrangian-conj-scope}
The original formulation of this result stated a single
$(-1)$-shifted symplectic structure on~$C_g$.  The proved version
reveals two structures of different degrees: the Verdier pairing
gives $(-(3g{-}3))$-shifted on~$C_g$ itself, while the ambient cyclic
deformation problem gives $(-1)$-shifted on the formal moduli.  The
direct bar-side BV realization of the $(-1)$-shifted structure remains
conditional on Theorem~\ref{thm:shifted-symplectic-complementarity}.
See Remark~\ref{rem:ptvv-relation} for the compatibility of the proved
and conditional realizations.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Completion kinematics and the modular cumulant transform}
\label{subsec:completion-kinematics-programme}
\index{completion kinematics|textbf}
\index{cumulant coalgebra|textbf}
\index{modular cumulant transform|textbf}

The completion-tower theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}) resolves the formal
MC4 obstacle.  What remains is a \emph{kinematic} theory of the
completed dual: the canonical primitive sector, the growth law of bar
windows, and the entropy of completion.  This subsection records the
programme; the full definitions appear in
\S\ref{subsec:completion-kinematics-cumulant}
(Chapter~\ref{chap:koszul-pairs}) and the explicit calculations
in \S\ref{sec:w-completion-kinematics}
(Chapter~\ref{chap:w-algebras}).

\subsubsection*{Kinematics versus dynamics}
\label{sss:kinematics-dynamics}

The completed bar-cobar theory separates cleanly into two axes
(Remark~\ref{rem:kinematics-dynamics-split}):
\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{Completion kinematics}: the primitive cumulant quotient
  $Q(\cA) = \bar\cA / \partial\bar\cA$
  (Definition~\ref{def:primitive-cumulant-quotient}), the primitive
  generating series $G_\cA(t) = \tfrac{1-t}{t}(\chi_\cA(t)-1)$
  (Definition~\ref{def:primitive-generating-series}), the completion
  Hilbert series $H_\cA(t) = G_\cA(t)/(1-G_\cA(t))$
  (Definition~\ref{def:completion-hilbert-series}), the primitive
  defect $\Delta_\cA(t) = G_\cA(t) - G_\cA^{\mathrm{naive}}(t)$
  (Definition~\ref{def:primitive-defect-series}), and the completion
  entropy $h_K(\cA) = \log(\rho_\cA^{-1})$
  (Definition~\ref{def:completion-entropy}).  These depend only on the
  vacuum character, not on OPE coefficients or curvature.
\item \emph{Modular dynamics}: the coderivation $D_\cA$, the
  curvature $\kappa(\cA)$, the universal MC class $\Theta_\cA$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}), and the dg-shifted Yangian
  kernel $r_\cA(z)$.  These depend on the full OPE structure.
\end{itemize}
The Virasoro involution $c \mapsto 26-c$ changes the dynamic data
but preserves the kinematic data: the same-family shadow
$\operatorname{Vir}_{26-c}$ lives on the dynamic axis.
Kinematically, even generic Virasoro has infinitely many primitive
cumulants (the defect $\Delta_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)$ begins $t^3 +
2t^5 + \cdots$).

\subsubsection*{The $\Walg_N$ entropy ladder}

The completion entropy forms a monotone sequence
(Proposition~\ref{prop:wn-entropy-ladder}):
\[
h_K(\Walg_2) \approx 0.567
\;<\; h_K(\Walg_3) \approx 0.772
\;<\; h_K(\Walg_4) \approx 0.835
\;<\; \cdots
\;<\; h_K(\Walg_\infty) \approx 0.872.
\]
The $\Walg_\infty$ character admits a MacMahon factorization
$\chi_{\Walg_\infty}(q) = \phi(q)\,M(q)$, where
$M(q) = \prod_{n\geq 1}(1-q^n)^{-n}$ is the plane-partition
generating function.  The $\Walg_\infty$ completion frontier is
governed by plane-partition combinatorics.

\subsubsection*{The modular cumulant transform (conjectural target)}
\label{sss:modular-cumulant-transform}

The \emph{cumulant coalgebra}\label{def:cumulant-coalgebra}
$\operatorname{Cum}_c(\cA) := \hat{T}^c(sQ(\cA)^\vee)$ is the
completed cofree coalgebra on the desuspended dual of the primitive
cumulant quotient $Q(\cA) = \bar{\cA}/\partial\bar{\cA}$
(Definition~\ref{def:primitive-cumulant-quotient}).

\begin{conjecture}[Cumulant recognition; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:cumulant-recognition}
For admissible~$\cA$ satisfying reduced-weight finiteness and
finite-window stabilization,
$\operatorname{gr}_\rho \hat{B}(\cA) \simeq
\operatorname{Cum}_c(\cA)$
as completed curved dg coalgebras.
\end{conjecture}

The platonic ideal of the completion programme is a single object
\begin{equation}\label{eq:modular-cumulant-transform}
M(\cA) = \bigl(\,
  \operatorname{Cum}_c(\cA),\;
  D_\cA,\;
  \tau_\cA,\;
  r_\cA(z),\;
  \Theta_\cA
\,\bigr)
\end{equation}
whose five components are:
\begin{enumerate}
\item $\operatorname{Cum}_c(\cA)$: the completed cofree coalgebra on
  primitive cumulants (the kinematic core);
\item $D_\cA$: the completed coderivation encoding genus-$0$ Koszul
  duality;
\item $\tau_\cA$: the universal twisting morphism (the local
  dynamical field);
\item $r_\cA(z) = \tau_\cA|_{\deg 2}$: the ordered
  $E_1$/Yangian face, satisfying the $A_\infty$ Yang--Baxter
  hierarchy;
\item $\Theta_\cA$: the connected all-genera modular logarithm,
  the stable-graph exponential
  $\Theta_\cA = \sum_{\Gamma\,\text{connected}} \frac{\hbar^{g(\Gamma)}}{|\operatorname{Aut}(\Gamma)|}\,\Phi_\Gamma$,
  satisfying the modular quantum master equation
  $d\Theta_\cA + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta_\cA,\Theta_\cA] + \hbar\,\Delta\Theta_\cA = 0$.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
\textbf{Status.}  Components (1)--(2) are controlled by the
completion-tower theorem and reduced-weight windows.  Component~(3)
is the bar-cobar twisting morphism, proved on $\CompCl(\Fft)$.
Component~(4) is the Yangian jet tower, accessible windowwise by the
jet principle (Conjecture~\ref{conj:jet-principle} below): reduced-weight-$q$
bar windows determine Yangian jets through order~$z^{-q}$.
Component~(5) is the principal open structural problem (MC2 is proved
at all finite orders; the full modular QME is conjectural in the
completed tensor product).

\begin{conjecture}[Jet principle; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:jet-principle}
\index{jet principle}
Reduced-weight-$q$ bar windows $K_q(\cA)$ determine the dg-shifted
Yangian MC kernel $r_\cA(z) = \sum_{m \ge 0} r_m\, z^{-m-1}$
through jet order~$z^{-q}$: that is, the truncation
$r_\cA(z) \bmod z^{-q-1}$ depends only on
$\barB(\cA)|_{K_q}$.
\end{conjecture}

\noindent
\textbf{Six shadows.}  Every shadow the monograph computes is a
projection of~$M(\cA)$:
\begin{enumerate}
\item genus-$0$ face $\to$ bar/cobar and Verdier duality;
\item ordered-boundary face $\to$ RTT/Yangian/dg-shifted Yangian;
\item all-genera face $\to$ modular homotopy theory;
\item scalar shadow $\to$ $\kappa(\cA)\lambda_g$;
\item spectral shadow $\to$ $\Delta_\cA(x)$, $\Pi_\cA$;
\item Lagrangian shadow $\to$ shifted-symplectic complementarity.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{conjecture}[Grand completion; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:grand-completion}
The modular cumulant transform $\cA \mapsto M(\cA)$ extends
finite-stage chiral Koszul duality to an equivalence between the
completion closure of admissible chiral $A_\infty$-algebras on curves
and the homotopy theory of complete pronilpotent modular cumulant
coalgebras, with genus-$0$ truncation $=$ completed bar/cobar,
ordered-boundary truncation $=$ dg-shifted Yangian jet tower, and
universal deformation theory $=$ graph MC
class~$\Theta_\cA$.
\end{conjecture}

\subsection{The analytic completion programme}
\label{subsec:analytic-completion-programme}
\index{analytic completion!programme}

The proved algebraic engine operates in the world of formal
factorization algebras, cochain complexes, and dg categories.  A
genuine local-to-global field theory also requires analytic sewing
(convergent partition functions, Hilbert-space completions, and
positivity).  Recent work of
Moriwaki~\cite{Moriwaki26a, Moriwaki26b} constructs conformally flat
factorization homology valued in $\operatorname{IndHilb}$ by left Kan
extension from conformally flat disk algebras; for the Heisenberg
VOA, the conformally flat 2-disk algebra on
$\operatorname{Sym} A^2(D)$ (the symmetric algebra of the Bergman
space) is identified with the ind-Hilbert completion of the affine
Heisenberg vertex algebra.  Adamo--Moriwaki--Tanimoto~\cite{AMT24}
prove conformal Osterwalder--Schrader axioms for a class of unitary
full VOAs under energy/spectral growth and local $C_1$-cofiniteness.

The programme aims to bridge the algebraic engine to these analytic
structures.  Its objects are the \emph{sewing envelope}
$\cA^{\mathrm{sew}}$ (the Hausdorff completion for the locally convex
topology generated by sewing-amplitude seminorms), the \emph{analytic
bar coalgebra} $\barB^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA)$ (graph-norm closure of the
algebraic bar), and the \emph{analytic shadow}
$Q_g^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA) := D^{\mathrm{co}}(
\barB_g^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA)\text{-comod})$.  At genus~$g$ with
curvature $\mcurv{g} \neq 0$, the coderived passage of
\S\ref{subsec:coderived-ran} is mandatory: ordinary cohomology fails,
and the correct receptacle is the coderived analytic category.

Four target theorems define the programme
(Chapter~\ref{ch:genus-expansions},
\S\ref{sec:analytic-completion}):

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\Alph*$_{\mathrm{an}}$)}]
\item \emph{Heisenberg sewing theorem}
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-sewing}): the sewing envelope
  of the algebraic Heisenberg VOA is exactly
  $\operatorname{Sym} A^2(D)$; the completed bar differential is
  the closure of the Gaussian collision operator on Bergman tensors;
  every closed amplitude is a Fredholm determinant on the
  one-particle Bergman space
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-one-particle-sewing}: one-particle
  Bergman reduction).
\item \emph{Lattice sewing envelope}
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:lattice-sewing}, \textbf{promoted from conjecture}):
  every positive-definite even lattice admits a canonical sewing envelope
  with charge-refined Hilbert sectors.  Proof: HS-sewing
  (Corollary~\ref{cor:hs-sewing-standard-landscape}),
  amplitude factorization as Heisenberg Fredholm determinant times
  Siegel theta function (classical convergence for
  $\operatorname{Im}\Omega > 0$), Bergman-space charge-sector completion.
\item \emph{Analytic realization criterion}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:analytic-realization}): a unitary full VOA
  satisfying conformal OS, polynomial spectral growth, and
  HS-sewing admits a sewing envelope, a conformally flat 2-disk
  algebra, and a higher-genus coderived shadow.
\item \emph{Boundary bar duality}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:boundary-bar-duality}): for an
  analytically Koszul~$\cA$, completed boundary modules at
  genus~$0$ are equivalent to analytic comodules over
  $\barB^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA)$; at curved genus, the correct
  objects are analytic contramodules over the curved dual.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
\emph{Status.}  Target~(A$_{\mathrm{an}}$), the Heisenberg sewing
theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-sewing}), is \ClaimStatusProvedHere{}
for clauses~(ii)--(iv) and \ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere{} for
clause~(i) (Moriwaki~\cite{Moriwaki26b}).  Target~(B$_{\mathrm{an}}$), lattice sewing
(Theorem~\ref{thm:lattice-sewing}), is \ClaimStatusProvedHere{} (promoted from conjecture).
Targets (C$_{\mathrm{an}}$) and~(D$_{\mathrm{an}}$) remain \ClaimStatusConjectured{}.
The programme is recorded here to fix definitions and the precise
relationship to the algebraic proved core.

\subsection{The universal Maurer--Cartan class}

The genus tower $\{\barB^{(g)}(\cA)\}_{g \geq 0}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:master-tower}) is controlled by a universal
obstruction.

\begin{theorem}[Universal MC class;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:universal-MC}
\index{Maurer--Cartan class!universal}
For a modular Koszul chiral algebra $\cA$ with non-degenerate
invariant pairing, there exists a class
\[
\Theta_{\cA} \;\in\;
\operatorname{MC}\!\left(
  \operatorname{Def}_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\cA)
  \;\widehat{\otimes}\;
  R\Gamma\!\left(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,\bullet},\, \mathbb{Q}\right)
\right)
\]
controlling the full genus tower as a single Maurer--Cartan deformation,
with three properties:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Its image under the scalar trace is the sequence of obstruction
  coefficients: $\operatorname{tr}(\Theta_{\cA})
  = \sum_{g \geq 1} \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g$.
\item It is compatible with clutching:
  $\xi^*(\Theta_{\cA})
  = \Theta_{\cA} \star \Theta_{\cA}$
  under the boundary maps
  $\xi \colon \overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g_1,n_1+1} \times
  \overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g_2,n_2+1} \to
  \overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$.
\item Under Verdier duality:
  $\mathbb{D}(\Theta_{\cA}) = \Theta_{\cA^!}$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This is Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-theta}, proved via the
assembly of Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-full-resolution}: the cyclic
$L_\infty$-algebra $\Defcyc(\cA)$ is constructed by
Theorem~\ref{thm:cyclic-linf-graph}, the completed tensor product
converges with clutching by
Proposition~\ref{prop:geometric-modular-operadic-mc}, and the
tautological line support $o_g = \kappa \lambda_g$ is established
by Theorem~\ref{thm:tautological-line-support}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope]\label{rem:universal-MC-scope}
The scalar shadow $\kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g$ is established
(Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}).  The clutching compatibility
is implicit in the modular operad structure of the bar complex
(Theorem~\ref{thm:prism-higher-genus}).  At the one-channel level,
Proposition~\ref{prop:tautological-line-support-criterion} shows that
these two geometric inputs would already force tautological-line
support once they separate the relevant sector, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-verdier-criterion} reduces the
remaining duality flank to a $\sigma$-stable Lagrangian two-plane on
that sector.  Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-ptvv-criterion} then
reduces the remaining H-level lift to perfect one-channel projector
subcomplexes whose cross Verdier pairing is a PTVV quasi-isomorphism,
and Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-chain-model-criterion} reduces
that lift further to explicit one-channel coderivation subcomplexes in
$\Defcyc(\cA)$ and $\Defcyc(\cA^!)$.  Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-seed-criterion}
then reduces those subcomplexes further to finite low-bar-length
cyclic coderivation seeds in
$\operatorname{CoDer}^{\mathrm{cyc}}(\widehat{\barB}_X(\cA))[1]$ and
$\operatorname{CoDer}^{\mathrm{cyc}}(\widehat{\barB}_X(\cA^!))[1]$.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-minimal-seed-packet-criterion}
compresses those finite seed sets further to one distinguished
degree-$2$ cocycle on each side together with bar-length-$\leq 3$
correction packets and a finite pairing matrix.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-visible-lowarity-packet-criterion}
then identifies the remaining packet with the three visible low-arity
ingredients already supported by the current MC2 surface: the
simple-pole bracket sector, the normalized double-pole pairing matrix,
and the Killing $l_3^\eta$ sector.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-canonical-transfer-criterion} then
reduces that visible packet further to a canonical transfer package on
the one-channel seed spaces: one cyclic seed, one shared
generator-seed lift producing the Killing $l_3^\eta$ sector, and one
functorial normalization splitting off the one-channel cocycle line.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-transfer-law-criterion} then reduces
that canonical package further to an explicit root-string transfer law
on those seed spaces: the genus-$2$/genus-$3$ profile
\[
O_2=t^2(ae_{12}+bf_1-mf_2),
\qquad
O_3^\eta=a m t^3\eta,
\]
together with obstruction-side recovery of $(a,b,m)$ and the same
coefficient-extraction normalization.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-root-string-chart-criterion} then
reduces that explicit law further to a chart-existence/uniqueness
statement: the ordered root-string chart is forced by the one-channel
support graph and normalization data, up to rescaling of the three seed
lines.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-intrinsic-line-detection-criterion}
then reduces that chart statement further to intrinsic line detection:
the seed, simple-pole, and Killing support lines must be canonically
picked out by $l_{2,\mathrm{sp}}$, $\beta_g^{\mathrm{dp}}$,
$\nu_g^{\mathrm{sp}}$, and the support of
$(O_{2,g},O_{3,g}^\eta)$.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-automorphism-rigidity-criterion}
then reduces that remaining line-detection step to automorphism
rigidity: those support lines are the unique invariant lines for the
one-channel support automorphism group compatible with the bracket,
pairing, normalization, and obstruction profile.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-support-graph-stabilizer-criterion}
then reduces that rigidity statement further to a finite stabilizer
computation on the labeled one-channel support graph: the fixed
vertices must be exactly the simple-pole, residual-kernel, and Killing
support lines.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-incidence-orbit-criterion}
then reduces that stabilizer statement further to an explicit
incidence-matrix / orbit-count computation on the visible one-channel
graph: the relevant support lines are exactly the singleton orbits of
the permutation group determined by the bracket, pairing,
normalization, and support indicators.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-visible-orbit-table-criterion}
then reduces that bounded permutation problem further to a universal
three-case visible orbit table on the
$m=1,2,3$ root-string types, equivalently
$\mathfrak{sl}_3,\mathfrak{sp}_4,\mathfrak{g}_2$.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-canonical-universal-orbit-table-criterion}
then collapses that three-case verification to direct
lookup/identification against one fixed labeled orbit table.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-universal-invariant-signature-criterion}
then collapses that fixed-table identification further to the minimal
visible invariant signature packet forcing that table.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-signed-seed-character-criterion}
then collapses that invariant packet further to the universal signed
seed-character law recovering it.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-two-sign-plus-normalization-scalar-criterion}
then collapses that character further to the reduced datum of two
root-string signs and one normalization scalar.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-parity-sign-plus-normalization-scalar-criterion}
then collapses that reduced datum further to one root-string parity
sign plus one normalization scalar.
Proposition~\ref{prop:one-channel-parity-forcing-criterion}
then collapses that parity-sign datum further to one chart-normalized
seed scalar.
The scalar-saturated class $\Theta_{\cA}$ is now constructed
for one-channel families
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-full-resolution}): (a)~the cyclic
deformation complex $\operatorname{Def}_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\cA)$
exists as a cyclic $L_\infty$ algebra
(Theorem~\ref{thm:cyclic-linf-graph}); (b)~the Maurer--Cartan
equation in the completed tensor product with tautological classes
is solved at the scalar level by the conjunction of
Proposition~\ref{prop:geometric-modular-operadic-mc} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:tautological-line-support}.
The non-scalar content is developed through the shadow
Postnikov tower
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-postnikov-tower}): finite-order
shadows through arity~$4$ are proved constructively, and the
all-arity convergence is guaranteed by the bar-intrinsic
construction (Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic};
Theorem~\ref{thm:recursive-existence}).
Scalar saturation (one-channel universality) is proved
for all algebras in algebraic families with rational OPE
coefficients (Theorem~\ref{thm:algebraic-family-rigidity}),
covering the entire standard Lie-theoretic landscape at
all non-critical levels including admissible ones.
The proof bypasses module-category semisimplicity via
Whitehead reduction to a finite-dimensional linear system
and algebraic semicontinuity of rank.

\emph{Homotopy template} (Convention~\ref{conv:hms-levels}): Type~I
(existence of a homotopy object).  At H-level: a filtered cyclic $L_\infty$
algebra $\operatorname{Def}_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\cA)$ and an MC element $\Theta_\cA$
with trace, clutching, and Verdier compatibility.  The scalar shadow is
$\kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g$ (proved, Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}).
The full non-scalar class is Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-theta}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:master-theta}).

The bar-intrinsic construction
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}: $\Theta_\cA := D_\cA - d_0$)
supersedes the original formulation with simple Lie symmetry: it
requires only a non-degenerate invariant pairing, with no restriction
on the symmetry type.  The simple-Lie version is a special case.
\end{remark}

\begin{conjecture}[Categorical modular Koszul duality;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]%
\label{conj:categorical-modular-kd}%
\index{modular Koszul duality!categorical}%
For each genus~$g$ and each modular Koszul chiral
algebra~$\cA$, the curved bar-cobar adjunction at genus~$g$
induces an equivalence
\[
\mathsf{D}^{\mathrm{co}}
\bigl(\barB^{(g)}(\cA)\text{-}\mathsf{comod}\bigr)
\;\simeq\;
\mathsf{D}^b\bigl(\cA\text{-}\mathsf{mod}^{\Sigma_g}\bigr)
\]
between the \emph{coderived category}
\textup{(}\S\textup{\ref{subsec:coderived-ran})} of curved
$\barB^{(g)}(\cA)$-comodules and the bounded derived category of
$\cA$-modules twisted by the Hodge data of~$\Sigma_g$.
This equivalence varies over $\mathcal{M}_g$ as a flat functor:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item At $g = 0$, it reduces to bar-cobar inversion
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion})}.
\item Applied to integrable representations of
  $\widehat{\fg}_k$, the functor $H^0$ recovers the
  Tsuchiya--Ueno--Yamada space of conformal blocks
  \textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:chain-vs-classical-mf})},
  and its monodromy gives the KZ/Hitchin connection.
\item The scalar shadow
  $\mathrm{obs}_g(\cA) = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g$
  is Theorem~D; the full Chern character
  $\mathrm{ch}(\mathcal{V}_g)$
  recovers the spectral discriminant~$\Delta_{\cA}$
  \textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:spectral-characteristic-programme})}.
\item Under Verdier duality:
  $\mathsf{D}^{\mathrm{co}}(\barB^{(g)}(\cA^!)\text{-}\mathsf{comod})
  \simeq
  \mathsf{D}^{\mathrm{co}}(\barB^{(g)}(\cA)\text{-}\mathsf{comod})^{\mathrm{op}}$.
\end{enumerate}
This is the \emph{categorical lift} of
Theorems~A--D to all genera: Theorem~B
gives the equivalence, Theorem~D gives its first Chern class,
and the full equivalence is the modular functor of~$\cA$.
\end{conjecture}

\subsection{The primitive kernel programme}
\label{sec:concordance-primitive-kernel}
\index{primitive kernel!concordance}

The cofree-coderivation principle (Milnor--Moore for modular operads)
compresses the full MC element $\Theta_\cA$ to its primitive
restriction $\mathfrak K_\cA \in \operatorname{Prim}^{\log}_{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$.
The primitive master equation
(Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-to-global-reconstruction})
\[
d\,\mathfrak K_\cA + \mathfrak K_\cA \star \mathfrak K_\cA
+ \hbar\,\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}(\mathfrak K_\cA) = 0
\]
carries three channels: the differential~$d$, the primitive
pre-Lie product~$\star$ (separating sewing), and the BV
self-contraction~$\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}$ (non-separating genus
raising).

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{Downstream results.}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Per-family primitive kernels.}
  The primitive kernel of each standard family is computed in the
  example chapters:
  \begin{center}
  \renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
  \begin{tabular}{llcc}
  \textbf{Family} & $\mathfrak K_\cA$ &
  \textbf{Channels} & \textbf{Ref.} \\
  \hline
  Heisenberg & $K_{0,2} + K_{1,1}$ &
  $\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}$ &
  Prop.~\ref{prop:heisenberg-primitive-kernel} \\
  Affine $\widehat\fg_k$ & $K_{0,2} + K_{0,3} + K_{1,1}$ &
  $\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}},\; [-,-]$ &
  Prop.~\ref{prop:affine-primitive-kernel} \\
  $\beta\gamma$ & $K_{0,2} + K_{0,4} + K_{1,1} + R_{\mathrm{pf}}$ &
  $\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}},\; \operatorname{Rig}$ &
  Prop.~\ref{prop:betagamma-primitive-kernel} \\
  Virasoro/$\mathcal{W}_N$ & $K_{0,2} + K_{0,3} + K_{0,4} + K_{1,1} + R_{\mathrm{pf}} + \cdots$ &
  all three &
  Prop.~\ref{prop:virasoro-primitive-kernel}
  \end{tabular}
  \end{center}

\item \emph{Shell equations as genus-forcing mechanism.}
  The primitive shell equations
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:primitive-shell-equations}) express
  the genus-$g$ data as a sum over three channels.
  Per-family:
  Heisenberg (Proposition~\ref{prop:heisenberg-primitive-shell}),
  affine (Proposition~\ref{prop:affine-primitive-shell}),
  $\beta\gamma$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:betagamma-primitive-shell}),
  Virasoro (Proposition~\ref{prop:virasoro-primitive-shell}).

\item \emph{Branch BV finite-rank reduction.}
  The branch master action $S_\cA^{\mathrm{br}}$
  (Definition~\ref{def:reduced-branch-master-action}) on the
  finite-rank quotient $V_\cA^{\mathrm{br}}$ satisfies the QME
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:branch-master-equation}).
  Per-family:
  Heisenberg (Computation~\ref{comp:heisenberg-branch-bv}:
  Gaussian, $\dim V^{\mathrm{br}} = 1$),
  affine (Computation~\ref{comp:affine-branch-bv}:
  Chern--Simons-type, $\dim V^{\mathrm{br}} = \dim\fg$),
  $\beta\gamma$ (Computation~\ref{comp:betagamma-branch-bv}:
  Gaussian on weight-changing line),
  Virasoro (Computation~\ref{comp:virasoro-branch-bv}: infinite
  series on primary slice).

\item \emph{Metaplectic half-density.}
  $\delta_\cA^2 = \Delta_\cA$
  (Corollary~\ref{cor:metaplectic-square-root}):
  $(1 - \kappa x)^{1/2}$ for Heisenberg,
  Weyl denominator for affine, genuine power series for Virasoro.

\item \emph{Flat connection and conformal blocks.}
  The MC equation defines a flat connection
  $\nabla^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA = d + [\Theta_\cA, -]$ on the
  modular convolution algebra
  (\S\ref{sec:flat-connection-intro}).  Its flat sections over
  $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ are the conformal blocks.  The chain
  \[
  \mathfrak K_\cA
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\operatorname{FT}^{\log}_{\mathrm{mod}}\;}
  \Theta_\cA
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\text{linearise}\;}
  \nabla^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\text{flat sections}\;}
  \operatorname{CB}_g(\cA)
  \]
  recovers the KZ connection (affine), Hitchin connection
  (Virasoro), and trivial connection (Heisenberg) as special cases.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{The discriminant as spectral invariant}
\index{discriminant!spectral invariant}

The shared discriminant $\Delta(x) = (1 - 3x)(1+x)$ across
$\mathfrak{sl}_2$, Virasoro, and $\beta\gamma$ systems
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ds-bar-gf-discriminant}) has a structural
explanation.  It is the \emph{first nontrivial non-scalar
characteristic class} of the modular Koszul object: where
$\kappa(\cA)$ is a scalar measuring the curvature of $d^2$,
the discriminant $\Delta_{\cA}(x)$ records the branch geometry
of the dual Hilbert series.

Distinct chiral theories can lie on the same modular spectral
sheet, sharing the same $\Delta$, even when their local
operator content is entirely different.  The underlying reason
is functorial: Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction changes the growth pole
(i.e.\ the leading OPE data) while preserving the discriminant
family.  This is compatible with the observation that
$\Delta_{\cA}$ depends only on the quadratic OPE data, which is
the Koszul-dual-determining datum.

\begin{theorem}[Discriminant as spectral determinant, verified cases;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:discriminant-spectral-verified}
\index{discriminant!spectral determinant}
For $\cA \in \{\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2,\, \mathrm{Vir},\,
\beta\gamma\}$, the bar-cohomology discriminant satisfies
\[
\Delta_{\cA}(x) \;=\; \det(1 - x\, T_{\mathrm{br}})
\]
where $T_{\mathrm{br}}$ is a $d \times d$ matrix whose eigenvalues
are the reciprocals of the branch points of the algebraic Koszul
dual Hilbert series $P_{\cA^!}(x)$, with $d$ the degree of
algebraicity.
In all three cases $d = 2$, the branch points are $x = 1/3$
and $x = -1$, and
$\Delta(x) = (1 - 3x)(1 + x)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Each of the three Hilbert series involves $\sqrt{1 - 2x - 3x^2}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ds-bar-gf-discriminant}):
$P_{\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2}$ and $P_{\mathrm{Vir}}$ satisfy
quadratic equations with discriminant $(1+x)(1-3x)$, while
$P_{\beta\gamma}^2 = (1+x)/(1-3x)$ has the same branch locus.

The branch points of any algebraic function $P(x)$ satisfying
$a(x)P^2 + b(x)P + c(x) = 0$ are the zeros of
$\mathrm{Disc}_P = b(x)^2 - 4a(x)c(x)$.  For
$\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$, the algebraic equation is
$x(1+x)P^2 - (1+x)P + 1 = 0$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ds-bar-gf-discriminant}), giving
\[
\mathrm{Disc}_P = (1+x)^2 - 4x(1+x) = (1+x)(1-3x).
\]
The branch points are $x_1 = -1$ and $x_2 = 1/3$.
Setting $\alpha_i = 1/x_i$, we obtain $\alpha_1 = -1$ and
$\alpha_2 = 3$, and
\[
\det(1 - x\,T_{\mathrm{br}}) = (1 - \alpha_1 x)(1 - \alpha_2 x)
= (1+x)(1-3x) = \Delta(x).
\]
Since $P_{\mathrm{Vir}}$ and $P_{\beta\gamma}$ involve the same
radical $\sqrt{1-2x-3x^2}$, they share the same branch locus,
hence the same~$\Delta$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Spectral discriminant, general case;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:discriminant-spectral}
\index{discriminant!transfer matrix}
\index{discriminant!spectral determinant!general case}
Let $\cA$ be a Koszul chiral algebra whose Koszul dual Hilbert
series $P_{\cA^!}(x) = \sum_{n \geq 1} \dim(\cA^!)_n\, x^n$
is either:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Rational}: $P_{\cA^!}(x) = N(x)/D(x)$ with
$\gcd(N,D) = 1$, $D(0) = 1$, and $\deg D = r$; or
\item \emph{Algebraic of degree $d \geq 2$}: satisfying an
irreducible $f(x,y) \in \mathbb{Q}[x,y]$, $\deg_y f = d$,
with discriminant $\Delta(x) = \operatorname{Disc}_y(f)$
normalized so that $\Delta(0) = 1$.
\end{enumerate}
Define the \emph{transfer matrix} $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$ as follows.

\emph{Rational case.}
The coefficients $a_n = \dim(\cA^!)_n$ satisfy a
constant-coefficient linear recurrence of order~$r$
(the degree of the denominator).  Let $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$
be its companion matrix.  Then $\Delta_{\cA}(x) := D(x)$ and
\begin{equation}\label{eq:discriminant-spectral-rational}
\Delta_{\cA}(x) \;=\; \det\!\left(1 - x\, T_{\mathrm{rec}}\right).
\end{equation}

\emph{Algebraic case.}
The coefficients $a_n$ satisfy a $P$-recursive recurrence
of order~$d$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:p-recursive-recurrence}
q_d(n)\, a_n + q_{d-1}(n)\, a_{n-1} + \cdots + q_0(n)\, a_{n-d} = 0
\end{equation}
where $q_i(n) \in \mathbb{Q}[n]$.  Let $c_i = \lim_{n \to \infty}
q_i(n)/n^{\deg q_d}$ be the leading asymptotic coefficient of~$q_i$
\textup{(}so $c_d = 1$ after normalization\textup{)}.
The asymptotic companion matrix is
\[
T_{\mathrm{rec}} =
\begin{pmatrix}
-c_{d-1} & -c_{d-2} & \cdots & -c_0 \\
1 & 0 & \cdots & 0 \\
\vdots & & \ddots & \vdots \\
0 & \cdots & 1 & 0
\end{pmatrix}
\in \mathrm{Mat}_{d \times d}(\mathbb{Q}).
\]
Then the bar-cohomology discriminant satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:discriminant-spectral-general}
\Delta(x) \;=\; \det\!\left(1 - x\, T_{\mathrm{rec}}\right).
\end{equation}
In both cases, the eigenvalues of $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$ are the
reciprocals of the singularities \textup{(}poles or branch
points\textup{)} of~$P_{\cA^!}$, and the spectral
radius of $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$ equals $\dim\mathfrak{g}$ for
Kac--Moody algebras
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:dominant-branch-point})}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Rational case.}
Write $D(x) = \prod_{i=1}^{r}(1 - \alpha_i x)$ with
$\alpha_i = 1/x_i$ the reciprocal poles.
The partial-fraction decomposition of
$P = N/D$ shows that $a_n = [x^n]P$ satisfies a
constant-coefficient linear recurrence of order~$r$
with characteristic polynomial
$\chi(t) = \prod(t - \alpha_i)$.
The companion matrix $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$ has $\chi$ as
its characteristic polynomial, so
$\det(1 - x\,T_{\mathrm{rec}}) = \prod(1 - \alpha_i x)
= D(x) = \Delta_{\cA}(x)$.

\emph{Algebraic case.}
The argument combines three classical results from analytic
combinatorics.

\emph{Step~1: Algebraic $\Rightarrow$ $P$-recursive.}
An algebraic power series is $D$-finite
(\cite{FlajoletSedgewick}, Proposition~VI.1), hence its
coefficients satisfy a $P$-recursive (holonomic) recurrence
of order~$d$, giving~\eqref{eq:p-recursive-recurrence}.

\emph{Step~2: Singularities of the generating function.}
Since $P(x)$ is algebraic of degree~$d$ with minimal polynomial
$f(x,y) = 0$, its singularities as an analytic function are
the branch points: the roots $x_1, \ldots, x_m$ of
$\Delta(x) = \operatorname{Disc}_y(f)$
(\cite{FlajoletSedgewick}, Theorem~VII.8).

\emph{Step~3: Poincar\'e--Perron theorem.}
For the $P$-recursive recurrence~\eqref{eq:p-recursive-recurrence}
with asymptotic companion matrix~$T_{\mathrm{rec}}$, the
Poincar\'e--Perron theorem
(\cite{FlajoletSedgewick}, Theorem~VIII.4)
identifies the eigenvalues of $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$ with the
asymptotic growth rates of the solutions: provided
$c_0 \neq 0$ and the eigenvalues $\alpha_1, \ldots, \alpha_d$
have distinct absolute values, the fundamental system of
solutions satisfies
$a_n^{(i)}/a_{n-1}^{(i)} \to \alpha_i$ as $n \to \infty$.

\emph{Step~4: Growth rates = reciprocals of branch points.}
By the transfer theorem for algebraic singularities
(\cite{FlajoletSedgewick}, Theorem~VI.3), the contribution
of a simple branch point~$x_j$ to the coefficients is
$[x^n]\, P(x) \sim C_j \cdot x_j^{-n} \cdot n^{-3/2}$.
The growth rates are therefore $\alpha_i = 1/x_i$, the
reciprocals of the branch points.

\emph{Synthesis.}
Combining Steps~3 and~4, the eigenvalues of $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$
are $\alpha_i = 1/x_i$.  Since $x_1, \ldots, x_m$ are the
roots of~$\Delta$ (Step~2) and $\Delta(0) = 1$:
\[
\det(1 - x\, T_{\mathrm{rec}})
= \prod_{i=1}^d (1 - \alpha_i x)
= \prod_{i=1}^d \Bigl(1 - \frac{x}{x_i}\Bigr)
= \Delta(x). \qedhere
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope and verification]%
\label{rem:discriminant-spectral-scope}
\index{discriminant!Poincar\'e--Perron}
The rational case is unconditional (given rationality of~$P$);
the algebraic case additionally requires the Poincar\'e--Perron
non-degeneracy condition ($c_0 \neq 0$, eigenvalues of distinct
absolute value).  Both conditions hold for all bar-cohomology
sequences computed in this work.  The residual conjecture is
that $P_{\cA^!}$ is algebraic or rational for all Koszul chiral
algebras associated to simple~$\mathfrak{g}$.

\emph{Algebraic verification $($degree~$2)$.}
For $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$, Virasoro, and $\beta\gamma$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:discriminant-spectral-verified}), $P$ is
algebraic of degree~$2$.
The Riordan recurrence
$(n{+}1) a_n = (2n{-}2) a_{n-1} + (3n{-}6) a_{n-2}$
gives leading coefficients $c_2 = 1$, $c_1 = -2$, $c_0 = -3$,
and $T_{\mathrm{rec}} = \bigl(\begin{smallmatrix} 2 & 3 \\ 1 &
0 \end{smallmatrix}\bigr)$ with eigenvalues $3$ and $-1$.
Check: $\det(1 - x\,T_{\mathrm{rec}}) = 1 - 2x - 3x^2
= (1-3x)(1+x) = \Delta(x)$.  The eigenvalue
$3 = \dim(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ is the exponential growth rate
(Theorem~\ref{thm:dominant-branch-point});
$-1$ reflects the alternating correction from the central
extension.

\emph{Rational prediction for $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3$.}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:sl3-bar-gf} predicts that
$P_{\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3}$ is \emph{rational} with
denominator $(1-8x)(1-3x-x^2)$, so the theorem applies
in its rational form with $r = 3$ poles.
The companion matrix of the recurrence~\eqref{eq:sl3-bar-recurrence}
has characteristic polynomial $(t-8)(t^2-3t-1)$, giving
eigenvalues $8$, $(3+\sqrt{13})/2$, $(3-\sqrt{13})/2$.
Check: $\det(1 - x\,T_{\mathrm{rec}})
= (1-8x)(1-3x-x^2) = \Delta_{\mathfrak{sl}_3}(x)$.
The spectral radius is $8 = \dim(\mathfrak{sl}_3)$,
consistent with Theorem~\ref{thm:dominant-branch-point}.
The remaining eigenvalues
$(3 \pm \sqrt{13})/2$ are the roots of the DS discriminant
factor $t^2 - 3t - 1$, shared with the $\mathcal{W}_3$ generating
function (Remark~\ref{rem:two-discriminant-families}).

\emph{Why not the Kodaira--Spencer operator on $H^1$?}
A natural first guess is
$\Delta(x) = \det(1 - x\, T_{\mathrm{KS}} \mid H^1)$
where $T_{\mathrm{KS}}$ acts on
$H^1(\bar{B}(\cA)) \cong \mathfrak{sl}_2$ ($3$-dimensional).
But Schur's lemma forces $T_{\mathrm{KS}}$ to be scalar on the
irreducible adjoint, giving $\det = (1-cx)^3$, degree~$3 \neq 2$.
The correct object is $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$ (dimension~$d$, the
degree of algebraicity), not~$H^1$ (dimension~$\dim\mathfrak{g}$).
Identifying a natural \emph{subquotient} $H^{\mathrm{red}}_1
\subset H^1$ on which a geometric operator recovers
$T_{\mathrm{rec}}$ remains open
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:discriminant-ks-operator}).

The discriminant's role as first non-scalar characteristic class
of the modular characteristic hierarchy parallels $\kappa(\cA)$ as the first
scalar characteristic number of the universal Maurer--Cartan
class $\Theta_{\cA}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-MC}).
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Spectral branch object]
\label{def:spectral-branch-object}
\index{spectral branch object|textbf}
\index{discriminant!branch transport operator}
A \emph{spectral branch object} for a modular Koszul chiral
algebra~$\cA$ is a finite-rank perfect complex~$V_{\cA}^{\mathrm{br}}$
together with a \emph{branch transport operator}
$T_{\mathrm{br},\cA} \colon V_{\cA}^{\mathrm{br}} \to
V_{\cA}^{\mathrm{br}}$ such that
\begin{equation}\label{eq:discriminant-det}
\Delta_{\cA}(x)
\;=\;
\det\!\bigl(1 - x\, T_{\mathrm{br},\cA}\bigr).
\end{equation}
The pair $(V_{\cA}^{\mathrm{br}}, T_{\mathrm{br},\cA})$ satisfies:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\Delta_{\cA^!} = \Delta_{\cA}$
  (the spectral discriminant is self-dual);
\item exact factorization functors preserving quadratic OPE data
  preserve $T_{\mathrm{br},\cA}$;
\item $\operatorname{rank}(V_{\cA}^{\mathrm{br}})$
  equals the degree of algebraicity of the Koszul-dual
  Hilbert series.
\end{enumerate}

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Status.}
In the verified cases (Theorem~\ref{thm:discriminant-spectral-verified}),
$V_{\cA}^{\mathrm{br}}$ is constructed as the span of the
companion-matrix eigenvectors of $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$,
and~\eqref{eq:discriminant-det} is proved.  The general
construction of $V_{\cA}^{\mathrm{br}}$ from the bar complex
(rather than from the recurrence) remains open; see
Conjecture~\ref{conj:discriminant-ks-operator} for the
conjectural identification with a subquotient of~$H^1$.
(Part of the MC2 theorem package; Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-full-resolution}.)
\end{definition}

\begin{computation}[Spectral discriminants of standard families;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:spectral-discriminants-standard}
\index{spectral discriminant!standard families}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\textbf{Family} & $\Delta_\cA(x)$ & rank \\
\hline
$\cH_k$ & $1-kx$ & $1$ \\[2pt]
$\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_k$ &
  $\dfrac{(1-kx)(1-(k{+}4)x)}{1-2x}$ & $2$ \\[6pt]
$\mathrm{Vir}_c$ &
  $1-\dfrac{c-26}{2}\,x$ & $1$ \\[6pt]
$\mathcal W_3{}_c$ &
  $\bigl(1-\dfrac{c-50}{2}\,x\bigr)
  \bigl(1-\bigl(\dfrac{c-50}{2}+\dfrac{48}{5c+22}\bigr)x\bigr)$
  & $2$ \\[6pt]
$\beta\gamma$ & $1+2x$ & $1$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The zeros of $\Delta_\cA(x)$ are the \emph{branch points}
of the modular MC problem: values of the spectral parameter
where deformation directions merge.  Poles are resonance
points where the tangent complex degenerates.

For $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$: zeros at $x=1/k$ and
$x=1/(k{+}4)$ (Feigin--Frenkel dual levels); pole at $x=1/2$
(critical level $k=-2$, where the center acquires opers).

For $\mathcal W_3$: two zeros at $x_1=1/\kappa_c$ and
$x_2=(5c{+}22)/(\kappa_c(5c{+}22){+}48)$, reflecting the
two-dimensional deformation space $(T,W)$.  At $c=50$:
$x_1\to\infty$, $x_2=3/2$.

For $\beta\gamma$: the unique standard family with
$\kappa<0$.  Branch point at $x=-1/2$; the genus tower has
alternating signs.

\emph{Duality.}
$\Delta_{\cA^!}(x)=\Delta_\cA(x)$ for all Koszul pairs:
the spectral discriminant is self-dual.  For
$\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$: the zero at $1/k$ corresponds
to level~$k$; the zero at $1/(k{+}4)$ corresponds to the
dual level $-k-4$.  The product of the two zeros is
$1/(k(k{+}4))$; their sum is $(2k{+}4)/(k(k{+}4))=2/k+2/(k{+}4)
\to 0$ as $k\to\infty$.

\emph{Rank.}
$\operatorname{rank}(\Delta_\cA)
=\deg\Delta_\cA
=\dim H^1_{\mathrm{cyc,prim}}(\cA)$: the number of independent
genus-$1$ deformation directions.  Rank~$1$ for algebras with
one-dimensional deformation space (Heisenberg, Virasoro,
$\beta\gamma$); rank~$2$ for $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ and
$\mathcal W_3$.
\end{computation}

\subsection{The index theorem for genus expansions}

The appearance of the $\hat{A}$-genus in the Heisenberg genus
expansion (Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-generating-function})
and the Bernoulli asymptotics of $F_g(\cA)$ are not coincidental:
they are the output of a Grothendieck--Riemann--Roch computation
on the universal curve.

\begin{theorem}[Family index theorem for genus expansions;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:family-index}
\index{index theorem!modular deformation|textbf}
